to the Judgment of the Sheep and the Goats? Also, trying to determine how his bridal model would work with this
model of the outer darkness presented problems. Dillow takes a soteriological bridal model; whereas, I adopt a

is more likely, then his bridal soteriology is strained in that it would not be consummated with all believers, as some
believers are cast into the outer darkness at this time. Understandably, later, in his 20th edition, Dillow reversed
himself and instead of saying that the bride was conducted to the nuptial chamber possibly at the end, he now stated
that it was “probably at the beginning” (p. 798). This is where I located it in my models. For this discussion, I am
using the traditional seven-years model, just as I did in TOD. In my more recent books, however, I have adopted
the ten-year model, which anticipates that the seven-year tribulation will not start until three years after the rapture.
        Incidentally, if I followed Tanner’s thesis, then my proposal in Darkness, that the effects of the Bema
judgment would not be carried out until the unfaithful believers were cast out of the city, would have had less
logistical problems in that the Bema would not occur until the effects of the Bema were ready to be carried out.
That is, the Bema would not occur until the beginning of the millennial state and the effects of the Bema would be
implemented immediately. Adopting Tanner’s proposal as to the time of the Bema, therefore, would have posed no
problem for my misthopology in that regard. In fact, it would have strengthened my position. But at present, I only
mention that as a possibility, as in the part one of this series I am more inclined to interact simply with Dillow’s
model (especially since my newer models in the latter part of this series allows me to retain the traditional location
of the Bema and consummation at the beginning and yet pose the immediate carrying out of the results pertaining
to the outer darkness, as we will see). Nevertheless, if a misthopoligist were inclined to pursue Tanner’s perspective,
then, rather than pose that the believers in all dispensations will inhabit New Jerusalem, a misthologist simply could
stipulate that only faithful believers from the various dispensations will inhabit the city.
     As to Dillow’s position, however, another obstacle encountered in interacting with Dillow’s migratory
treatment is that in his second 2012 edition (p. 801) he also made a distention between the marriage in Rev 19:7 (in
Heaven) and the subsequent marriage supper in Rev 19:9 (on earth). This discussion in that section is gone from
the 2013 edition, and instead a cursory chart is provided in the 2013 edition that places Rev 19:7-9 as occurring in
Heaven (p. 828). I am left to wonder if Dillow simply removed some of these details from his treatment as a result
of our interaction because the details caused problems for his bridal soteriology. Having the foolish believers
included in v. 7 but excluded from v. 9 is certainly problematic for Dillow’s bridal position. Did Dillow jettison the
exegetical details of his 2012 edition (pp. 799-801), in regard to the distinction between the verses and the singular
versus plural forms of gamos and gamoi as discussed in that section, in order to retain his strained bridal soteriology?
He retains the gamos-gamoi distinction in the background (p. 815) but not in his exegesis. Indeed, in that discussion
he reversed himself by inserting a new phrase and deleting previous statements. The 2012 edition said, “The formal
wedding supper (Revelation 19:9) occurred toward the end of the week of wedding celebration and the gamoi
(festivities) which proceeded it occurred in heaven in the New Jerusalem” (p. 790). The implication of the
bolded text is that Rev 19:9 occurs on Earth after Christ’s return, which is consistent with his exegesis of Rev 19:6-
9 of that 2012 edition:

            Since Revelation 19:7 refers to a gamos and Revelation 19:9 refers to deipnon tou gamou (the
      supper of the feast), it seems reasonable to conclude that a distinction is implied....
            ....the marriage ceremony (gamos) mentioned in Revelation 19:7 occurs in heaven and is
      followed by the [sic.] Christ’s return to earth with His bride to celebrate the Wedding Supper of the
      Lamb [Revelation 19:9] at the beginning of the millennium” (p. 801; emphasis his).

My charts that I supplied to Dillow via email were based on this distinction. This information was removed from
his 2013 edition. Instead, Dillow made a reversal: “The formal wedding supper (gamos, Revelation 19:9) occurred
toward the end of the week of the wedding celebration, just prior [to] the second coming” (p. 815). Later, he
removed this statement in the 20th edition (p. 815). The 2012 edition split the verses and placed Rev 19:9 as
occurring after the second coming. The 2013 edition lumped Rev 19:7 with 19:9 as occurring prior to the second
coming. Evidently, after I pointed out the bridal problems for Dillow in his separating the two verses, he decided to
join them together in order to retain his bridal model. Naturally, given my bridal misthology, I am more inclined to
gravitate toward his earlier distinction made in the 2012 edition between Rev 19:7 and 19:9. Nevertheless, an author
must be allowed to adjust his arguments in order to try and gain consistency, so I will accept Dillow’s lumping the
two verses together as a working premise for his position when I interact with his attempt to try and justify his bridal
soteriology later in this series. See “Models for the Bride” in Part 3.
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                     Page 21
misthological bridal model. Nevertheless, I was hopeful that he might be able to find a way to work out any
inconsistencies in his models so as to pose an internally consistent alternate bridal model to my own. Scientifically,
I am open to competing misthological models as long as they are internally consistent misthologically and externally
consistent soteriologically.

                                                      Gehenna
       For example, I welcomed Dillow’s temporal-misthological model for Gehenna. Scientifically, I found it to
be a beautiful competing model to my own classical model. In Darkness, I present evidence in favor of a classical
temporal-soteriological model for Gehenna. Still, I laid the ground work for a neoclassical model that would
combine my classical model with Dillow’s new model so as to derive a neoclassical synthesis. My classical model
and his neo-Dillowian model need not be mutually exclusive. For example, Hodges has interpreted the OT warnings,
as employed in Hebrews and James, to be exclusively temporal. However, many of his fellow misthologists, myself
and Dillow included, perceive these warnings to have eschatological (i.e., misthological) dimensions as well, as
used by these NT writers. A dual dimensionality is thus perceivable. Likewise, one might argue that Dillow’s focus
on the temporal nature of Gehenna need not be so thoroughgoing as to disallow an eschatological dimension as
well. Indeed, in opening up the OT temporal aspect of judgment to picture the NT Bema, Dillow has conceded this
point in principle. The question that remains is if the eschatological dimension is to be understood exclusively in
misthological terms or if a soteriological aspect might be entailed as well. In my neoclassical model, I had
synthesized his neo-Dillowian model with the classical model so as to pose a neoclassical model in which temporal
Gehenna has dual eschatological dimensions, applying misthologically to unfaithful believers and soteriologically
to unbelievers. I find his competing Gehenna model, therefore, to be very attractive and complementary to my own
classical model.

                                                Marriage Supper
       Consequently, in our correspondence I was trying to picture how Dillow’s bridal soteriology might be made
to work with his darkness misthology. The complexity in comparing his model with mine was increased in that we
also have two different models for the marriage feast. As seen in the illustration above, he had proposed that the
marriage feast (in Heaven) was followed by the marriage consummation (in Heaven) and then followed by the
marriage supper (on Earth). In the beginning, I thought that he was anticipating that the unfaithful believers cast
into the outer darkness would be excluded from the Marriage Supper. Dillow clarified that this was not his intention.
Rather, the whole bride (soteriologically composed of all believers within his model) would participate in the
consummation and supper. Accordingly, I corrected my original adaptation of his original model in the illustration
below.
Page 22                                                                                  Misthological Models Part 1
                                 Illustration 5. Correction of Original Adaptation




        Thus, this corrected adaptation now more closely approximates Dillow’s original projection.42 Even so, the
tension remains in placing all of the Bride within the bridal chamber and part of the Bride within the outer darkness.
If such spatial distinctions are indeed involved, then the tension is very pronounced. How could the Bride be both
excluded from and included in the bridal activities? Part of Dillow’s solution was to pose that the exclusion and
inclusion are not concurrent. Rather, the exclusion is followed by inclusion. In his model both (1) the weeping on
the part of the foolish believers and (2) their separation from the bridal festivities last only for seven years.
Correspondingly, the profound regret that unfaithful believers experience as a result of the exclusion is limited to
the time of the tribulation (i.e., the Marriage Feast). Obviously, this caused severe tension with his placing the Bema
after the seven years. How could they experience a punitive Bema after their tears already had been dried away?
Bema in the Middle
       Because of the problems associated with locating the Bema at the conclusion of all the marriage activities in
his original proposal, Dillow experimented within his model with moving the Bema from Earth to Heaven at the
conclusion of the seven years. After all, as scientists we must be free to experiment with various models in order to
see what models better accord with the data. By placing the Bema before the Marriage, he would be able to entertain
the possibility that all believers are allowed into the Marriage as part of the Bride, in accordance with his
soteriological bridal model.

       Experimenting with this revised model revealed logistical problems, however. Not all misthologists accept
the premise that rewards are eternal, but this is a fundamental premise that both Dillow and I share in our respective
models. In his Gehenna model at that time, temporal Gehenna misthologically would represent the temporary
postmortem judgment on unfaithful believers. In other words, Gehenna represents the Bema. Just as the fire of the
Bema is temporary (Jn 15:6; 1Cor 3:15), so the fire of Gehenna is temporary. However, even in this revised model,
being cast into the outer darkness and weeping were still temporary, pre-Bema events. I attempted to chart where
the temporary and eternal misthological aspects might be located in his experimental model. The following chart
provides the gist of that discussion.

       On the one hand, posing that the outer darkness is temporary is an attractive option in view of the parabolic
imagery in Mt 22:13, in which being bound and cast out of the Marriage Feast that night would be a temporary
outcome. Even if Dillow were to follow this temporary perspective, though, favored by some of our misthological
peers, it still would pose a problem in that casting into the outer darkness in these parables seems to be a result of
the Bema rather than a pre-Bema event.
Bema First
       For such reasons, Dillow moved the Bema to the classical position in his next model in that he placed the
Bema before the Marriage Feast, and thus before any of the marriage activities. On the other hand, because his
marriage model has the marriage feast spanning the entire seven years, his placement of the Bema at this location
is not entirely classical. The classical position would not only place the Bema first but conceive of it as taking place
during the first half of the tribulation. One need not suppose, however, that Dillow’s model would not allow time
for the Bema. To the contrary, some dispensationalists believe that there will be months, even years, after the rapture
before the tribulation starts on Earth. For example, Crawford follows Berner in placing the Ezekiel Wars as taking
place on Earth during the gap of time between the rapture and start of the tribulation. Through their joint influence,
I eventually came to adopt this model myself. Bill Salus has popularized this view.43 Plus, my full model, as
discussed in Darkness, poses that the Heavenly City will be encased in a time bubble to allow the Bema to take
however long it needs while events are slowly unfolding on Earth at a far slower pace. After all, as we know from
the theory of relativity, time is relative. In any case, Dillow’s posing that the Bema takes place before the tribulation
is not a problem in terms of having enough time for the judgment of the Bema to be rendered.

       At this juncture, I also modified my adaptation of Dillow’s proposed model to coordinate it with both my
model regarding a possible association with Ezekiel’s Temple and my adaptation of Becker’s model.44 As already
noted in Darkness, Becker has posed that unfaithful believers will live inside the New Jerusalem: “Those who are
born again by the Spirit but fail to hear God and obey will live inside the heavenly city but receive no reward.”45 In
my reconstruction of her model, presuming that believers currently are in the city as they await judgment, her model
would divide the city into three sections and limit subcomers to the lower one. In my mind this would have been
equivalent to saying that the outer darkness is within the lower level. Becker, however, did not make this association
since she mistook the outer darkness for a soteriological theme. Moreover, she mistakenly (or at least inconsistently)
thought that unfaithful believers would be able to eat of the tree of life.
       In Darkness, I could have interacted further with her model by posing that the outer darkness is inside New
Jerusalem, just as Dillow did in Destiny, but I chose not to do so because I concurred with the Misslers: “Being

thrown into the outer darkness is probably not something that occurs in heaven, but something that occurs on the

was that the effects of the Bema judgment would not be carried out until the unfaithful believers were cast out of

of unfaithful believers who lived within the lower third of the city, she did not have a good way to implement this
limitation. I modified her model for this Dillowian adaptation so as to project that the tree of life would be limited
to the upper two-thirds of the city. The tree line of this mountain city would be such that the tree is not found in the
lower third where those in the outer darkness dwell. Thus, this heavenly tree line would operate inversely to earthly
tree lines. In our mountains on Earth, the tree line marks the upper limit of tree growth. Inversely, per this model,
the tree line in the Heavenly City would mark the lower limit of tree growth. Naturally, the table fellowship would
also be limited to those in the upper two-thirds of the city. Additionally, in accord with my TOD models, I located
the springs of water of life as originating from the top of the city where the throne of the Bema is located.48
Millennial and Eternal States
       Having come up with a working model of the outer darkness that would accord with Dillow’s marriage model
during the tribulation, the next part of the project was to complete the model by considering the implications of
such a model on one’s understanding of the millennial and eternal states and, in particular, answer the nagging
question: “What happens to unfaithful believers who are cast into the outer darkness during the millennial and
eternal states?”

   Chuck and Nancy Missler, The Kingdom Power, & Glory: The Overcomers Handbook, new and revised edition

   In my newer model in part 4 of this series, I will suggest that the unfaithful never live inside the city. They may

   This neo-Dillowian proposal might be harmonized with Becker’s model by locating the outer darkness in the
lower section of the city. This proposal is attractive in that the effects of the Bema are carried out immediately. But
what about access to the tree of life, losing one’s portion in the city, and having direct access to the springs of the
water of life (Rev 7:17; 22:19)? These are rewards. How could access to these city privileges, which is limited to
overcomers, be denied to those who live within the city? Becker speculates that unfaithful believers are allowed
into the lower city but not permitted access to the streets where the tree of life is located. I found this argument
strained when I initially read it. Are not the streets throughout the city? Nevertheless, to advance this harmonization
of Dillow’s model beyond my initial impressions of the weakness in Becker’s prototype of his position, the proposal
might be entertained that although the streets are located throughout the city, the tree of life is only found by the
streets in the top two-thirds of the city. The tree line stops at the top of the first level of the city. No trees are found
below the second level. Thus, those who reside in the outer darkness within the lower level would not have access
to the tree of life. They would have lost their portion in the portion of the city where the tree of life grows.
Accordingly, they would have lost access to the springs of the water of life, presumably located at the top of the
city, where the Bema throne is located (Rev 22:1). The water of life flows from those springs throughout the city,
however, and would be freely available to those living in the lower section (Rev 21:6; 22:17). This misthology
harmonizes with FG soteriology: The water of life is free, but being led to the springs themselves from which those
waters originate is restricted to overcomers.
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                      Page 27
                                 Illustration 9. Eternal Residency within the City




       Since Dillow holds that unfaithful believers will have eternal residency (i.e., free residency) within the city,
the extrapolation for this part of his model was rather straightforward. I offered the above schematic of his position,
with adaptations from my model and Becker’s model. After all, now that he had made the outer darkness a post-
Bema result, it objectively would be an eternal result since rewards (both positive and negative) are eternal from
our joint perspective. He and I disagree, though, as to the duration of the subjective response to the Bema. Foremost,
I believe that unfaithful believers will regret their unfaithfulness for all eternity. Furthermore, I personally do not
believe that the promise of wiping away of tears applies to all believers. However, my misthological model
regarding the tears is unique. I could conceive of them shedding tears on occasion throughout eternity. Nonetheless,
regardless on our differences on these matters, our mutual agreement that rewards are eternal should, in theory at
least, make creating competing models on the objective spatial restrictions rather easy. The objective results of the
Bema are eternal. Consistency requires continuity between how his model deals with those cast into the outer
darkness both during the tribulation and after the tribulation. At this juncture Dillow inquired as to where I would
place unfaithful believers during the tribulation within my model.
Page 28                                                                                  Misthological Models Part 1
                                          Illustration 10. Classical Model




       My model of the outer darkness is classical in that it is basically an adaptation of the models of those who
have done the pioneering work on the misthological aspects of the outer darkness from the GES perspective. From
its inception, the theses by Huber and Sapaugh have conceived the marriage supper to represent the privilege of
rulership within the millennial kingdom. To be excluded from the supper, then, would be a misthological portrayal
of being excluded from this millennial rulership. Carmical had projected a spatial dimension to this exclusion,
picturing it as being confined to the South Pole during the millennium. Therefore, as I explained to Dillow, my
model in Darkness would not allow unfaithful believers to be cast into the outer darkness until the marriage
supper started, which in the classical model would be after the millennium commences. I also placed the Bema in
its classic dispensational location as taking place during the first 3½ years of the tribulation. Not until New
Jerusalem appeared above Earth during the millennium would the effects of the Bema be carried out so that those
unfaithful believers residing in the lower section of the city would be excluded from the city. With this explanation
in hand, Dillow then modified his model with an ingenious adjustment.49

       Dillow responded by combing his previous model with the classical location of the outer darkness as being
exclusion from the Messianic Banquet during the millennial kingdom. However, he retained his location of the
outer darkness during the tribulation. The net result was that he now had an exegetical basis for his projection
that the outer darkness was applicable both before and after the marriage!50 This modification was nothing
less than sheer genius on his part. At the same time, in accord with the classical model, he now moved the
Marriage Supper to Heaven. If his dual approach to the outer darkness in this regard is correct, and the preliminary
indications are very promising, then Scripture intends for us to see the results of the Bema denoted by the outer
darkness as being immediately applicable! One does not have to wait until the millennial kingdom starts to see
the effects of the Bema being carried out. For this reason, this modification is extremely intriguing. This model
appears to be internally consistent and thus a plausible competing model to the classical model. What is more, the
two models need not be mutually exclusive, or at least not entirely so.

questions to be explored in the present series are: “Where is the outer darkness?” and “When does the outer darkness
become applicable?”
50
   Unfortunately, Dillow did not follow through on the logical implications of his new position, however. Instead,
he still considers the outer darkness temporary, which is triple inconsistency. First, making the OD temporary is a
carryover from his old positioning of the Bema after the OD. Second, he affirms positive and negative rewards are
eternal, and the OD is a negative reward; hence; it is eternal. Third, he believes that those in the OD will still live
in the Heavenly City. Thus, he should have acknowledged that in his model the OD continues.
Page 30                                                                                    Misthological Models Part 1
                                         Illustration 12. Neoclassical Model




       If the classical model is combined with this neo-Dillowian model, one possible neoclassical model would
be to anticipate, in a manner consistent with my adaptation of the neo-Dillowian model, that those cast into
the outer court during the tribulation will be confined to the lower section of the city where the tree of life is
not available. In other words, the only real addition that needs to be made is to pose that those cast into the outer
court will be moved to the outside of the city to the outer darkness at the beginning of the Marriage Supper (i.e., at
the beginning of the millennium).51 After the city is revealed above the Earth during the millennial kingdom,
those previously cast into the outer court of the city will then be excluded from the city in a manner consistent

51

could be thousands of years, I would not label the lower level of the city as the outer darkness since I would not
picture what the Scripture terms with a negative connotation as the outer darkness (i.e., being excluded from
rewards) as being inside the Reward City. Further, living in the outer court is not necessarily a negative experience.
Other believers will be living there (such as infants, children). For them the outer court will be anything but a
negative experience. But being confined (pictured as being bound hand and foot, Mt 22:13) to the outer court as a
result of a negative outcome at the Bema would be a preliminary taste of the outer darkness. Those confined to the
outer court would not be able to visit the rest of the city or eat the tree of life found in the upper levels. Infants and
children, in contrast, although residing in the outer court where direct access to the tree of life is not available, will

with my classical model. This hypothesis accords very well with my classical proposal, in which the location of

outer darkness to the outside of the city when the rule of city expands to encompass the Earth. The lower level of
the city would not be left empty by this vacancy. My original projection, after all, was that the first level (i.e., the
outer court) of the city is for infants, children, immature believers, and subcomers. The departure of the latter will
not leave the lower level unoccupied. Rather, their departure simply will make room for visitors to the outer court.

in the outer court of the city and visiting the outer court would then have access to the tree in this lower region.

        One might even pose that the temple has dual applicability. The vertically oriented temple schematic, pictured
on the left side of the illustration, is using the temple in conjunction with the city to pose a possible labeling for the
three sections of the city. This schematic was then laid down flat and the labels replaced with visual components
(i.e., the city, planet, and outer space), pictured on the right sight of the illustration, to represent probable
applicability in the eternal state. Ergo, at last we now have a reasonably functional competing spatial model to the
classical model for the outer darkness, right? Probably not.
Dungeon in the Basement?
       The problem, that I had not thought to mention to Dillow when we were first discussing these models, was
the inquiry that led to our protracted email discussions noted earlier. The subject for those emails was the question:
“Where are the dead believers now?” I had supposed that Dillow’s fictional story about being teleported to the
Bema at the city square was an indication that they were teleported to the city from another location. If so, that
would mean that they are currently not in the city (or at least not in that part of the city). That model would work,
or at least seem to work, as well as can be expected by someone considering the outer darkness to be inside the
Heavenly City, which is a very strained perspective to a classical misthologist as myself. Still, I was interested in
seeing Dillow develop a sound competing model to my classical model. But Dillow evidently had anticipated that
dead believers are currently living with the Lord in the city, assuming it is a literal city. That model would seem too
implausible to be creditable. Assuming literal correspondences are involved, such a model would pose them being
brought up out of the basement of the city, so to speak, that is, the lower level of the city, only to be cast back into
the basement as their punishment. Not surprisingly, then, Dillow was shying away from assigning literal values
to the parabolic details! Quite frankly, I do not envision living in the lower section of that Heavenly City as being
an occasion for profound regret or for crying out, “Noooo.” Is being led outside the city square to the city basement
the equivalent of being led to a city dungeon (Mt 18:34) or being thrown misthologically into metaphorical
Gehenna? Perish the thought!
Where are dead believers?
       Yet I did not want to see a literal rendition of Dillow’s model perish. If he is correct that the Marriage
Feast occurs during the tribulation, then developing a working model for that perspective would be worth
the effort. For a solution to the dilemma, that is, to develop a literally feasible rendition of Dillow’s model, I turned
to my friend, Scott Crawford. In my classical model, as already noted, I had presumed that when believers die, they
go to be with the Lord in the Heavenly City. I did not pose that the lower section of the city is the outer darkness.
Rather, being cast into the outer darkness refers to the ejection from the city that occurs at the beginning of the
millennium. My classical model did not pose a metaphorical dungeon in the basement. Crawford would agree with
my model on the backend but would pose another model on the frontend. If his model is added to the frontend of
Dillow’s model, I believe we have a feasible competing model to my classical model.
       As already noted, Dillow’s fictional account of the Bema had made it seem that when it was time for the
Bema to start, all believers where teleported to the city from elsewhere: “Suddenly, there was a sound like the rush
of a great wind. In an instant millions of people abruptly appeared in the heavenly city. The dead in Christ had
risen. Those still living had received resurrection bodies, and all had been transported to heaven in the twinkling
of an eye” (p. 750). If this fictional story is allowed to have literal value, then where might it be posed that the dead
in Christ were before being teleported to the Heavenly City? As I mentioned to Dillow at the beginning of those
correspondences:

            The impression I get from this description is that you are anticipating that believers (even those
      who previously have died) will not be brought to the city until the rapture. My friend, Scott Crawford,
      holds such a view. Granted, in view of the fact that the bride would not be at the father’s house until
      fetched by the groom, I see how this position would be attractive from that perspective. But I have
      some problems, or at least some questions, if that is the case. If this indeed is the perspective you are
      adopting, where do you propose believers are now who die and are with the Lord?

      In response to this question, Dillow answered, “I would assume that saints today live there but then this
begins to raise additional questions about who lives there in the millennium because there are people living all over
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                        Page 33
                                                                                            52
the universe. I just am unable to construct a logical scenario that would hold up.” Thus, Dillow abandoned
hope for the literal model. Contrastively, in my opinion, retreating to a metaphorical city will not hold up. And
posing a literal city in which they were teleported out of the basement only to be cast back into the basement would
not hold up either. Dillow’s dilemma certainly was understandable. However, a third possibility was available—to
consider Crawford’s model. Crawford had not worked out the details for his model, but his suggestion was enough
to provide a foothold for a working premise for Dillow’s model. In response to my inquiry to Crawford, as to his
not believing that those who have died and gone on to be with the Lord are currently living in the city, Crawford
responded,

                Correct. I don’t believe believers are currently living in the city. They are with Christ, but
         not necessarily in the city. Now, I can’t get much more specific regarding their living quarters; and
         they may be in the city!?!? My reason for saying they do not live or abide in the city is due to it being
         a place of reward. And if believers have not yet been judged and have not received their reward, they
         would not enjoy the privileges of being a city dweller. Maybe they have limited access....say for
         worship time, but it seems tenuous to say they abide in the city.53
                                 Metaphorical Models for the Outer Darkness
      Before advancing to the development of a spatial Crawford-Dillow model, however, I would like to pause
and consider a metaphorical model, which is the model to which Dillow retreated. Dillow insists upon a
metaphorical city. Let us see how well that proposal will hold up to scientific scrutiny. As we now have seen, for
such a metaphorical model to be persuasive, it must deal with literal corresponding details in such a manner that
would be consistent with pre-Bema, Bema, and post-Bema locations for those who will be cast into the outer
darkness. For purposes of examining possible metaphorical models, I will assign a few values for our scientific
experimentation:

•     Let S (somewhere) be defined as where believers who have died and gone on to be with the Lord are now. After
      all, they have to be somewhere!
•     Let C (city) be defined as a nebulous location, metaphorically called a city. After all, this metaphysical place
      has to be someplace! This metaphorical city could be a cube, a plane, a pyramid; neither the shape, dimensions,
      nor name matter. The name city is simply being implemented for the sake of convention to refer to this literal
      location wherever it is.
•     Let OD (outer darkness) be some nebulous location, metaphorically called the outer darkness. After all, those
      cast into the outer darkness have to be cast someplace! This metaphorical darkness could be a cube, a plane, a
      pyramid; neither the shape, dimensions, nor name matter. The name outer darkness is simply being
      implemented for the sake of convention to refer to this literal location wherever it is.
•     Let B (Bema) be defined as the place where the Bema judgment will take place. After all, it has to take place
      someplace! The name Bema is simply being implemented for the sake of convention to refer to this literal
      location wherever it is.

       With these values in hand, we can now consider three hypothetical models by which Dillow might be able to
hold a metaphorical construction, bearing in mind that at least these four primary metaphorical components (S, C,
OD, and B) must have corresponding literal values, even in his metaphorical arrangement. In the diagram of these
three hypothetical models, the arrow below the ellipse represents activity happening in relation to Earth during this
time: Up (rapture), Horizontal (tribulation), Down (return).

                                         as to make Heaven the outer darkness!

         To summarize the three options, when believers are brought from somewhere inside of the city to appear
before the Bema, those cast into the outer darkness must either go: (model A) someplace else within the city,
(model B) the same place within the city, or (model C) nowhere and just remain where they are at in the city, that
is, at the Bema. In looking at the issue from a strictly metaphorical perspective, model B is the most probable option.
At the point of the rapture, those currently with the Lord are brought before the Lord from wherever they are now
in the city. If they are judged to be unfaithful, they are sent back to that same location. This location is somewhere
in Heavenly Jerusalem. Thus, the outer darkness is a part of the Heavenly City since in Dillow’s model unbelievers
are sent to the outer darkness during the tribulation.
         My objections to this model are several. First, there is manifold, independent, conformational evidence that
the city itself is a reward. For example, see my discussions of misthopology (reward city) in TOD. Even aside from
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                         Page 35
Matthew’s outer darkness, I would conclude from Psalms, Isaiah, Hebrews, and Revelation that the city is a Reward
City. Merely being allowed a permanent residence within that city is unquestionably a reward. Second, model B
does not adequately explain losing one’s right to the tree of life and table fellowship, etc., unless something
equivalent to my adaptation of the basement motif is added to this model. While it is possible that the city might
have the proposed tree line among other things, Occam’s razor would render such proposals superfluous in
comparison to the simpler, classical model. Third, the whole notion that the punishment effected at the Bema is to
be sent back to some place within the city is farfetched. Fourth, the fact that this darkness would be the same place
within the city where some believers have been spending the past 2000 years makes it all the more improbable.
Fifth, in Dillow’s own Gehenna model, as I pointed out in Darkness, the better option is to allow the fire of Gehenna
to represent the eternal consequences of the Bema rather than the Bema itself. The temporary Bema experience is
eternal in its result. Jesus graphically portrays this reality with the Jewish garbage dump. To be cast into Gehenna
was to be cast outside of the city, not inside of it! The garbage dump is not inside the city!
        As I explained to Dillow, while we were working on modifications to his model, someone like myself will
notice that his propensity to a metaphorical treatment of the parabolic details gives plenty of information by which
to deduce that the outer darkness must have spatial restrictions.
                                      Illustration 15. Nebulous Outer Darkness




        Per his own comments, the outer darkness is a restriction (of some type) within New Jerusalem from wherever
the literal sections denoted by the metaphorical city, hall, festivities, table, and bridegroom are located. Let the outer
darkness be defined as that nebulous area in New Jerusalem described by the parabolic metaphorical details. From
his analysis, we may note that he has not defined what parts of the city are excluded from the outer darkness;
nevertheless, the experiential parabolic exclusion he envisions must entail corresponding spatial restrictions of some
type, unless we are to adopt model C and make Heaven the outer darkness! And this deduction, that the outer
darkness necessitates that some type of spatial restrictions be deemed as necessary, has not even factored into
consideration the other data that he did not discuss, such as the tree of life and lost portion in the city, only to
mention two. Thus, in my adaptation of his position (i.e., the basement theory with no trees or table in the basement),
I am merely pointing out the most probable location of his own restrictions.
        Dillow was trapped by his own premise. Earlier he had asked me, “I wonder how you locate the outer
darkness outside of the New Jerusalem during the tribulation. There is no ‘outside’—it is in heaven and has
not yet descended to earth?”54 As I recounted to him, this was a very good question, an excellent one in fact.
However, in my model, as originally conceived (i.e., the classical model), there is no outer darkness during
the tribulation. The effects of the Bema, for the most part, are not carried out until the end of the tribulation in my
TOD model. Basically, because I adopted the classic view which places the consummation at the beginning of the
celebration, I held the typical view which places the marriage in Heaven and the wedding feast and supper on Earth.
The feast depicts the 1000-year reign. Thus, I was developing my model for the outer darkness in TOD within the
perimeters of the classic view of the outer darkness presented by previous GES writers on the subject. Since

54
     Personal correspondence, 12-16-2012.
Page 36                                                                                   Misthological Models Part 1
according to this classical model one is not cast out of the feast into the outer darkness until the feast commences,
one is not cast out until the millennial reign starts. So my hypothesis was that, as a result of the Bema, unfaithful
believers are sent (back) to the lower section of New Jerusalem until such time that the feast commences (i.e., during
the millennial reign), at which time they would be cast out of the city (and thus into the outer darkness).
       In Dillow’s new model, however, the feast takes place immediately after the Bema (once he moved the Bema
back to its original location which, as far as I could tell, was a logistical necessity). Since unfaithful believers are
cast into the outer darkness immediately after the feast starts, this means that, according to his model, they must
be cast into the outer darkness during the tribulation. Accordingly, Dillow was being entirely consistent
within his model to place the outer darkness inside New Jerusalem. In terms of logical consistency, then, given
our shared premise that there was no place outside the city into which unfaithful believers could be cast, this aspect
of his model was necessary—the Bema must be placed back at the original location, the beginning.

                   •    Classic model: Bema then Marriage then Feast then Outer Darkness
                   •    Neo-Dillowian model: Bema then Feast then Outer Darkness then Marriage

       At that time, my projection was that Dillow would need to keep the outer darkness within the city for eternity
in order to accomplish his objectives of making the city the free residence of all believers. And I concluded that he
would need to maintain free residency since he maintains that all believers are part of the Bride. It would not make
sense for him to have the Bride kicked out of her own house! Therefore, nothing would change in regard to the city
after the tribulation according to his model. What would change is that those in the outer darkness will not be able
to participate in the rulership that commences at that point. So part of the Bride rules; part does not. Granted, I
perceived this as being an internal inconsistency within his model. But the only way that I can see around this
obstacle is to acknowledge that not all believers will compose the Bride.55 Since this was not a concession Dillow
was willing to make, the best solution I could propose was to pose the above clarifications and hypotheses.
Nevertheless, since his preference for a soteriological Bride only seems to be a superficial appendix to his model, I
jettisoned the bridal component of his argument for my purposes. My objective was to try and assist in finding a
working model for his placement of the outer darkness during the tribulation. His model for the outer darkness
was attractive enough to be worth the effort. For if Dillow proves to be correct that the marriage feast spans the
seven years (or even the last 3 ½ years) of the tribulation, then I would need to adopt some form of the
neoclassical model concerning that prospect.
       For such reasons, I consulted Crawford. His model seemed to be the only way to rescue the neoclassical
model. Part of my epistemological approach is to consider the possibility that I might be wrong and to come up
with contingency models should that prove to be the case. Doing so is good science. So when I turned to Crawford,
I was willing to consider the possibility that both Dillow and I were wrong in our working premise, which was that
there was no place outside the city currently. My perception was that Dillow’s model would be severely strained,
and perhaps falter altogether, without implementing some such outside-the-city possibility and without retreating
to a metaphorical position (as unlikely as a metaphorical proposal would be). Dillow’s model had proven
unsuccessful in resolving this dilemma.
       So if we die before the Lord returns, from where will we be saying to Scott within his model, “Beam me up
to the Bema?” The light was finally beginning to dawn on me. The almost self-apparent answer was staring me in
the face: Outside the city of course! Heaven is bigger than the Heavenly City. The city is only part of Heaven.
The garbage dump is located outside of the city limits. That deduction is not exactly rocket science. So, as a scientist
considering various models, at last I was now willing to listen to Scott explain his model because, by my
calculations, some such model was needed to rescue Dillow’s model.
       After all these years, I finally was willing to listen to my good friend, Scott Crawford, share the details of his
model. Building models takes a lot of work, and in this simplified overview I am not even sharing all the calculations
that have to be undertaken. My fuller discussion in Darkness gives some idea as to how much work is involved.
The immediate problem I had with Scott’s outside-the-city model was, “Where would he pose that unfaithful

       In further conversation with Scott, he also suggested that in the case of the Rich Man and Lazarus, no pre-

in one location, and believers were in another. No grades of punishment for unbelievers would seem to be in effect,
and no grade of rewards for believers would seem to be in effect. Judgment is according to works. Until such
judgment takes place, placing believers in graduated levels within the Reward City would be improbable. How
would one determine what levels of the Reward City one would live in before the rewards had been rendered?
Therefore, in his model Crawford would place all believers in one location, where they would all be treated the
same until judgment is rendered. Occam’s razor certainly would be in his favor.

                                                           believers are then thrown into the same place (OD)
                                                           where they were originally, which is somewhere
                                                           outside the city.
                                                           Mathematical Summation: (S = OD) ⊄ C

                        Model C2                            When the Bema (B) occurs at the time of the rapture,

                                                           join raptured believers from Earth to appear before the

Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                          Page 39
                                              3D Neoclassical Model
       Of these alternate models, my preference is for Model B2, or a variation thereof, which is why I sought
Crawford’s clarification on that particular model—the courtyard model. I enjoy theoretical discussions just as much
as the next misthologist and have demonstrated, via 2D diagrams, that the conclusions being derived herein are
compatible with a metaphorical approach. Notwithstanding, having demonstrated herein that even a metaphorical
approach will lead to a spatial understanding of the outer darkness, I will return to 3D models for illustrative
purposes since Crawford and I both share a propensity for the literalicity of the city. Multiple variations are possible.
The following is but one possible rendition of a courtyard model.58
                                     Illustration 17. Present Location of the City




        At the present time, the city and its courtyard could be conceived as being at some remote distance from
Earth and in an alternate dimension. There is no need to think that the tree of life is limited to certain parts of the
city. Rather, as in the classical model, the whole city is virtually a greenhouse for this tree, but this tree is not found
in the courtyard outside the city. The outer darkness is currently not a place of punishment. Rather, as depicted in
2 Enoch, the outer darkness is simply an outer courtyard in front of the King’s palace, where those waiting that
night for the feast are gathered in joyful anticipation of the dinner soon to come. Quite possibly, Jesus alludes to
this literary background in His second parable concerning the outer darkness. Those believers currently living in
the courtyard of the city are eagerly and joyfully anticipating being able to enter the city when the rapture occurs.

58
  My interest in the courtyard model is not limited to the logistical considerations evidenced in the present book
but also factor into consideration the probable correlation of the outer court of Ezekiel’s temple typologically
portraying the outer darkness and the plausible intertestamental imagery of the outer court of Enoch providing the
backdrop for the second parable of the outer darkness. Moreover, the very nature of that parabolic imagery, even
apart from these three considerations, strongly indicates that the outer darkness is the outer courtyard in that parable.
These four factors provide grounds for seriously considering the courtyard model as a viable option. Logistical,
typological, intertestamental, and parabolical considerations coalesce for strong argument in favor of such a model.
Page 40                                                                               Misthological Models Part 1
                                   Illustration 18. Future Location of the City




      When the Lord comes to Earth at the time of the rapture, the city and its courtyard will be teleported to a
place near Earth but remained cloaked from view in an alternate dimensional, time bubble. As Dillow fictionally
portrays it but I literally apply it, both those church-age believers dwelling in the courtyard and those living on
Earth will be teleported atop the city to the Bema (at the city square) to be judged. Those believers found unworthy
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                      Page 41
of residing in the city will be cast back into the outer courtyard and thereafter permanently excluded from the city.
Some misthologists pose that these unfaithful believers will be able to enter the city but not have residence therein.
In my estimation, they will have neither residence nor access; they will never step foot inside the city again.
Regardless, realization of their forfeiture will cause them to weep and gnash their teeth. Since only church-age
believers are judged at this time, the remaining OT believers will await their day in court in the outer courtyard of
the city. The return of weeping church-age believers to the courtyard will give pause to those OT believers still
waiting in the courtyard. “Will they qualify for residency in the city when it is their time to be judged?” will be the
question foremost on their minds.
                                   Illustration 19. Ultimate Location of the City
Page 42                                                                                  Misthological Models Part 1

       At the conclusion of the tribulation, those believers who have not yet been judged (i.e., OT believers as well
as dead and living tribulational believers) will be gathered before the Lord at judgments that will take place on
Earth. The Jacobean Bema for the Jews will be followed by the Judgment of the Sheep and Goats. Those believers
found worthy of co-ruling with Christ will have city access, of course. Resurrected believers found unworthy of the
city will be cast back into the courtyard. Because rewards are eternal, the loss of rewards is eternal as well. The
outer darkness (i.e., the outer courtyard) will be the permanent residence of those unfaithful believers cast back into
it. Living tribulational believers who are found unworthy of ruling will remain on Earth and enter the millennial
kingdom in flesh and blood bodies and be sentenced to the courtyard at the conclusion of the millennium.59 The city
will be uncloaked and visible above Earth during the millennium, being removed from the dimensional bubble.
Evidently, the city courtyard will remain cloaked in the alternate dimensional bubble. Therefore, a reasonable
hypothesis is that the courtyard will be moved to an area below Earth at the commencement of the millennial
kingdom. Should another writer wish to write a fictional account of the Bema outcomes from the perspective of this
model, Carmical’s projection of the South Pole for the location of the outer darkness during the millennium would
have to be adjusted for such a model to include the outer courtyard motif. The southern hemisphere would be for
flesh and blood believers who survive the tribulation. At the conclusion of the millennium, the remaining unjudged
believers will be judged. Resurrected millennial believers found unworthy of rulership will be cast back into the
courtyard and thus reside in the outer darkness of the courtyard for eternity.
                                        Illustration 20. Crawfordian Model




59
  The ejection of unfaithful tribulational believers who survive the tribulation is not pictured on the chart.
Technically, they do not need to be pictured since they remain on Earth. More precisely, though, they will be
excluded from the Promised Land and perhaps have to reside in the lower hemisphere.
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                        Page 43

        A couple of points of clarification need to be made about my illustrations of Crawford’s position. I have
labeled the courtyard/outer darkness consistently in all three time periods: now, then, later. In relation to the
parabolic imagery that Jesus uses for the second occurrence of the outer darkness (with the possible Enochian
backdrop), it must be remembered that the outer darkness is simply the outer court (i.e., the courtyard) of the palace
where the feast is being prepared. Significantly, 2 Enoch also uses this imagery. Friends wait outside in the darkness
of the courtyard while dinner is being prepared inside the palace. To be cast into the outer darkness after dinner
starts simply would picture being cast back into the place where one was waiting before the dinner started—the
courtyard outside. The added detail of being bound hand and foot means that such outcasts would be restricted to
that courtyard, which is the original location where they were waiting before the feast started. In this Crawfordian
model, when believers die, they go to be with the Lord at Heavenly Jerusalem, but they do not reside in the Heavenly
City. Rather, they reside outside the city in eager anticipation of being able to take up residency inside the city once
it is completed, at which time (i.e., at the Bema) they will be assigned their quarters (within the city). Presumably,
they can see the construction going on at the city and possibly can even visit inside the city.
        Once the Bema commences, those believers found to be unfaithful will be cast back into this outer courtyard
(i.e., the outer darkness). In contrast to my reluctance to label this sector as the outer darkness in some of the
previous neoclassical models, until the effects of the Bema have been fully implemented, I have labeled this
courtyard as the outer darkness in this model, even in the current time period, because it is not inside the city. During
the tribulation and even during the millennium, this sector will function in both a positive and negative manner.
Those believers who die during the tribulation will reside in the courtyard until they are judged at the end of the
tribulation. Those believers who die during the millennium will reside in the courtyard until they are judged at the
end of the millennium. Those believers who do poorly at their respective judgment will be sent back to the courtyard
and sentenced to live there eternally.
        Incidentally, this courtyard should not be confused with the foundation of the city. Abraham was looking for
the city with foundations as his reward (Heb 11:10). Both the city and its foundation descend out of Heaven above
Earth (Rev 21:2,10-20). As to my theory that within the Crawfordian model the courtyard is separated from the city
during the millennial kingdom and eternal state, I have placed Earth in the center, between the city and its courtyard,
because there does not seem to be any obstacle between Earth and the Heavenly City (with its foundation) during
the millennial kingdom and eternal state.60 Also, this placement would correspond to the temple motif:

1. Holy of Holies—the city (with its foundation) is located above Earth.
2. Inner court—the planet is located (inter-dimensionally?) in-between the city and outer courtyard.
3. Outer court—the courtyard/outer darkness (possibly still cloaked in an alternate dimensional bubble) is below
   Earth.

       Several points in favor of the Crawfordian model may be briefly mentioned. First, unfaithful believers are
told that they will never enter the promised rest (Ps 95:11; Heb 3:11; 4:3,5). Consequently, among other things,
they are excluded from the City of Rest. Crawford’s model has an advantage over my classical model in that my
original TOD model would have all believers currently in the City of Rest, only to be excluded eventually and, at
that point, eternally. Granted, their works have not yet followed with them so as to qualify them to experience this
city as a place of rest/rulership (Rev 14:13), so in defense of my earlier model one might stipulate that they are in
the city, but it has not yet become the City of Rest for them. On the other hand, the typological precedence suggested
by the Exodus generation collaborates Crawford’s model. The unfaithful children of Israel were not living in the
Promised Land before they inherited it. Rather, they were waiting outside the Promised Land, along with the faithful
believers and the children below the age of accountability, until the judgment pronounced against the carnal
believers was completed while they were still in the wilderness. Being in the wilderness could be seen easily as a
picture of being in the outer court. Whereas in Crawford’s model they would never be allowed into the city, in my
classic model they would have spent the last 2,000 years in the city. His model is thus superior to my original model
60
   Indeed, in some popular models, the city is believed to come down and rest on Earth during the eternal state.
Placing Earth between the city and its courtyard would be very natural for those models. Also, this placement is
attractive in demonstrating that the classical model, as envisioned by Carmical, is not entirely mutually exclusively.
As an aside, both models could regard the unresurrected souls being depicted beneath the alter in Rev 6:9 as having
literal spatial representation.
Page 44                                                                                     Misthological Models Part 1
in that aspect. Historically also, the groom went to get the bride and bring her to his house. She was not living in
the bridal suite before being brought to his house! Additionally, intertestamental support can be derived from the
Enochian backdrop for the outer darkness as being the courtyard outside.61 Suffice it to say, the Crawfordian model
deserves careful consideration. The present study is only providing preliminary observations.
                                            Spatial/Metaphorical Summaries
        In conclusion, Dillow’s hypothesis that different groups of believers will be cast into the outer darkness on
separate occasions is valid. Dillow, Crawford, and I are agreed on that conclusion, regardless of which model is
employed. The real question is, “Will the first phase of this casting into the outer darkness (for church-age believers)
be delayed until after the tribulation?” If the feast for church-age believers occurs during the tribulation, as Dillow
proposes, then the answer is, “No, the exclusion will not be delayed.” Unfaithful church-age believers will be cast
into the outer darkness when they are found unworthy at the Bema. This casting will be after the rapture but before
the end the tribulation in both the Dillowian and Crawfordian models. My perception, in that case, is that Crawford’s
B2 model should be invoked to assist Dillow’s model. On the other hand, if the feast does not occur until after the
tribulation (with the result that the classical model is then the preferred model), then the answer is, “Maybe, perhaps
the exclusion will not be delayed.” The question at that point would be, “Which model is more probable, Crawford’s
model or my adaptation of Becker’s hypothesis concerning restriction in the lower sector of the city as the temporary
location of departed, unfaithful believers?” Even in its own right, Crawford’s B2 Model poses a splendid, competing
model to the classical model. At this juncture, then, misthologists have several working models for the outer
darkness to evaluate in further peer review. The strongest contenders would be: the classical model, the neoclassical
B2 model, or a combination of Crawford’s model with the classical model. Other variations are also possible.
        One such variation is pictured in Illustration 21. Crawfordian-Dillowian Composite Schema. Rather than
picture the outer darkness as being within the city, as Dillow originally proposed, this adaptation of Dillow’s model
has enlisted the aid of Crawford’s model to propose that, if during the tribulation church-age believers are cast into
what the Scripture terms with negative connotations as the outer darkness, this darkness metaphorically represents
the literal outer courtyard outside the city rather than the conjectural outer court inside the city. After the tribulation,
when the Messianic Banquet commences with the beginning of the millennial kingdom, resurrected unfaithful
believers from the OT and tribulational eras will be cast into this same darkness; although, it will now be relocated
to the south of this planet, albeit possibly in another dimension.




61
  Of course, in this same passage the king comes in and finds the unworthy guest “in here,” which most naturally,
given the paradigm by Crawford and myself, would be the Reward City (Mt 22:12). This parabolic detail, if pressed
to that extent, would be seen as supporting my model. Yet those who prefer the Crawfordian model might suggest
that being at the Bema atop the city might qualify sufficiently for this parabolic detail. Similarly, if they are at the
table before being cast out from the table in Mt 8:11-12, this would support my model’s placing them in the city
before being cast into the darkness. Both models have points in their favor.
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                           Page 45
                         Illustration 21. Crawfordian-Dillowian Composite Schema
Page 46                                         Misthological Models Part 1
          Illustration 22. Crawfordian Schema
Chapter 1. Models for the Outer Darkness                                                                        Page 47
        Crawford’s model is strong enough that it should be given independent consideration. For my classical model
in Darkness, I argued for a popular model in which paradise has been transferred to the Heavenly City. The only
minor clarification that would need to be made, to make such a perspective applicable to the Crawfordian model, is
to specify that the inhabitants of paradise have been moved to the courtyard of the city. Against the Crawfordian
model, it might be noted that in the parable of the wedding feast, Jesus does not depict the poorly dressed believer
as being cast out of the feast until after the feast has started. From a classical point of view, this means that this
outcast is not cast out until after the millennial kingdom has started. Thus, if this parabolic detail is assigned
chronological significance, it would pose a problem for Crawford’s model. How could this parable be understood
as dealing with unfaithful church-age believers being cast into the outer darkness before the millennial kingdom
commences, if Jesus is indicating that they are not cast out until after the millennial kingdom has started? Granted,
some misthologists, such as Dillow, would not find this to be an obstacle since they do not necessarily pose any
chronological significance to the details of the story. For classical misthologists, such as myself, however, who are
very much attuned to the plausibility of the parabolic details conveying eschatological significance, this parabolic
detail presents a considerable obstacle for Crawford’s model. In fact, this is one of the reasons that for many years
I was highly resistant to Crawford’s model.
        A breakthrough occurred, though, when, for other reasons entirely, I came to conclude that Jesus probably
intended for the parable of the wedding feast to have joint applicability to both church-age believers and tribulational
believers. Only much later did I realize that this dual perspective minimized, if not outright nullified, my resistance
to the Crawfordian model in regard to that particular parabolic detail. Originally, I did not pick up on this fact
because, as a classical misthologist, I anticipated that the unfaithful church-age believers and tribulational believers
would be excluded from the feast within the millennial kingdom after first being allowed into the feast within the
millennial kingdom. Exclusion from the feast would be postponed until after the millennial kingdom already had
started.62
        On the other hand, given Crawford’s overall model and the duality of my model for this particular parable,
one might allow that Jesus intends for us to make the classical extrapolation in terms of the parable’s applicability
to tribulational believers being cast out after the millennial feast starts but conclude that He did not intend for us to
limit ourselves to this singular perspective. Even if Dillow’s model is rejected (according to which the feast for
church-age believers occurs inside the city during the tribulation) in favor of the classical model (which postpones
the feast until after the tribulation), we are to understand that the same thing that happens to tribulational believers
(i.e., being cast out into the darkness outside after the feast has started) will occur to church-age believers (although
before the feast starts in the case of church-age believers). Although in Crawford’s model church-age believers will
be cast into the outer darkness before the feast starts, this does not prevent us from seeing that they will be further
removed from the city after the millennium kingdom starts, when the courtyard where unfaithful believers are
residing in the outer darkness will be moved to the other side of the planet, further away from the Heavenly City.
At this same time unfaithful tribulational believers will be cast into the outer darkness—after the feast starts.
Therefore, allowing for this duality means that Crawford’s model does not weaken the chronological applicability
of this parabolic detail. Any perceived weakness for his model will have to be sought elsewhere.
        In probing this model for weakness, a compound problem that immediately comes to mind is that Rev 7:9-
17 presents a group of believers serving day and night before what appears to be the throne within the Heavenly
City during the tribulation. If their residency inside the city is therein implied, how could these believers have
residency within the Heavenly City during the tribulation? One option for Crawford’s model is to adopt the
hypothesis that these victorious believers standing before the throne during the tribulation are rewarded church-age
believers who came out of the tribulation in the sense of being delivered from it.63 But if that is the case, how will
one deal with the souls beneath the alter (Rev 6:9-11)? Once again Berner poses that these are church-age saints;


62
   This parabolic detail would not present a problem for Crawford’s model in the case of those who interpret the

exclusive tribulational perspective do so in order to argue that tribulational Jewish unbelievers are the ones cast into
the outer darkness so that the outer darkness is a soteriological issue. I refute this argument in Darkness.
Nevertheless, even if it is dealing with the tribulational period exclusively, one should conclude that it is dealing
with believers cast into the misthological darkness.
