probably was wrong in simplistically assigning the last trumpet to the end of the church age. In the new model being
entertained herein, the Jewish-roots model, the last trumpet is still regarded as marking the end of the church age,
but not for the simplistic reasons I originally anticipated. I now allow that Dillow is very likely correct, 90% so, in
rejecting my simplistic dispensational explanation for this trumpet as ad hoc. But in this Jewish-root model, I now
believe that the last trumpet will announce the rapture of the church but not for the ad hoc reason posed by
dispensationalism. Therefore, the strength of my argument in assigning the last trumpet to the rapture is now much
stronger than it was in Darkness.
        The major drawback preventing me from adopting this perspective until now is the doctrine of imminency,
which affirms that the rapture can happen at any time. In my new model, I still affirm this perspective to some
degree. The probability of the rapture happening any day of any year is still 10%.20 But the probability of Jesus not
returning until the Feast of Tabernacles, of any given year, is inversely 90%. Moreover, given the historical
background, when Jesus said that no one knows the day or the hour except the Father, He probably was simply
affirming that it will be just like the father who tells his son that he can go rapture his bride. Only the father knew
the hour because the father monitors his son’s progress in preparing the new dwelling for his son’s soon-to-be bride
and determines when the construction is complete.
        This type of discussion naturally leads to the question, “Was the rapture imminent in Paul’s day?” I will
answer that question with a question, “Was the kingdom really near in Jesus’ day?” Perhaps the answer is both yes
and no. The dualistic answer depends on the perspective taken for the point of reference. The kingdom was near in
terms being a bona fide offer. The kingdom was at hand. Israel could have received the kingdom at that time if the
Jews had repented and believed the gospel (Mt 4:17; 10:7; Mk 1:15; Lk 10:9-10). Could they do so? Yes. Would
they do so? No. Did God know that they would reject it? Yes.21 As a result, God laid out a prophetic plan that
necessitates certain things that must happen before the kingdom is realized. For example, the ten-toe divided
kingdom must occur before the millennial kingdom will come to pass (Dan 2:42-44). Additionally, a ten-year Day
of the Lord (inclusive of the seven-year tribulation) must occur before the kingdom comes. Prophetically, then, the
millennial kingdom was not near or at hand because the OT predicts that a number of events will take place before
Israel enters into the millennial kingdom. Contingently, however, the kingdom was near and at hand because if
the Jews had repented (and they could have), then the Lord would have brought about the kingdom promptly. No
ten-toe division or ten-year wait would ever occur and the Danielic prophecies never would have been made in that
case.
        Similarly, this dualistic point of view allowed Paul and James, for example, to see the rapture as immanent;
it could happen at any moment. There were no contingencies that the church had to fulfill before the rapture
occurred. On the other hand, with the advantage of being able to put things into a historical perspective today, we
can see that, from a prophetic point of view, the rapture probably has not been imminent in terms of having all the
prophetic pieces in place until just now because of the timing with the contingencies and prophecies regarding
Israel. From the simple vantage point of the Lord coming for His Bride, the rapture could happen at any time—any
day, any year—once the heavenly preparations are completed. From the prophetic vantage point, though, as to when
the timing of His return for His Bride will occur in relation to other factors, particularly the Lord resuming His
exclusive dealings with Israel, the rapture almost certainly (e.g., 90% certainty) will not occur until the Feast of
Trumpets on any given year. As to which year, because of a number of prophetic models converging in the 2012-
2018 window, the rapture is more likely than not to occur before the end of 2018. Most emphatically, however,
prudence dictates that one not set absolute dates. Since I am more confident that the rapture will occur on the Feast
of Tabernacles (in terms of which day) than I am that it will occur by 2018 (in terms of which year), computing the
probability that the rapture will occur before the end of 2018 to be around 70% seems reasonable. Accordingly, I
anticipate that the last trumpet probably will occur within the next few years, not over a thousand years from now,
as Dillow proposes.
Prophetic Window
      Many believe that there will be 6000 years of post-Adamic human history, followed by 1000 years of the
millennial kingdom. The 6000 years are divided up into three 2000-year sections. The last 2000-year section marks
the Christian era. This model is falsified when calculated precisely using prophetic days. A modern year (MY) has

       Berner’s point is well received as a working hypothesis herein because dispensationally it holds up if not
calculated with a precision greater than that intended by the text. Specifically, Peter points out, “With the Lord one
day is as [hos] a thousand years, and a thousand years as [hos] one day” (2Pet 3:8). When hos is used with numbers
it means “a degree that approximates a point on a scale of extent, about, approximately” (BDAG). Peter is not
saying that a thousand years is one prophetic day with the Lord, only that it approximates one prophetic day. As
Berner notes in his book, “It is commonly recognized by both Jews and Christians that the prior six thousand years
of human history can be broken down into three segments of roughly two thousand years each.”25 For computational
purposes, a critical question would be, “How roughly?” Secondly, how rough the estimate is will be based on which
scale is used: PY versus MY.

within this 2015-2018 prophetic window. And with Iran becoming increasingly nuclear, the political landscape
seems to coincide with such expectations, following Bill Salus’ model, which seems very reasonable. So currently
I would project a probability of the rapture occurring in the 2017-2018 window as 70%, and thus 30% in 2019-2027
during this respective time frame. On the other hand, if in 2019 the rapture still has not occurred, then I would
project a 60% probability for the 2019-2027 window, and correspondingly 40% for 2028-3037 during that
respective time. If the rapture has not occurred by 2027, then the probability of such models is further diminished.
One might still give a slight elevation from these models and project a 55% probability from 2028-2067. If the
rapture still has not occurred by 2067, then the credibility of such models for computational purposes has been
falsified. Independently of other factors, the probability of the rapture would return to 50%, meaning that in terms
of numeric calculations derived from such cycles and patterns, the probability of the rapture would not be any
greater one day versus the next. A 50/50 possibility of the rapture occurring any given day would be the default
probability.33
Enoch’s 70 Generations
       Some use a passage in 1En 10:12 to predict when the Nephilim will return: “When all their sons kill each
other, and when they see the destruction of their loved ones, bind them for seventy generations, under the hills of
the earth, until the day of their judgement and of their consummation, until the judgement, which is for all eternity,
is accomplished.” Appealing to Ps 90:10, Horn computes 70 x 70 to derive a 490 year wait until their return, so he
appeals to 1En 10:12 to predict the return of the Nephilim in 2015-2017 A.D.34 The glaring problem with Horn’s
projection, however, is his math. He uses the Holocene Impact Working Group for scientific estimation of when
the flood occurred due to meteor impact: 2800-2900 B.C. He uses this same date range in his book. This would put
the range of return anywhere from 2000-2100 A.D. But in the videos, Horn inexplicably narrows this window to be
very soon, the immediate hour, occurring somewhere in 2015-2017 A.D. Not true—at least not from the date ranges
Horn is using.35 Fortson uses the same argument but implements better math. He places the flood at 2880-2900 B.C.
Thus, he predicts the return in 2000-2020 A.D. If the flood could be pinpointed with that much accuracy
scientifically, then Fortson’s projection would be reasonable.36
       Using the biblical genealogical records, on the other hand, some young Earth creationists would calculate the
flood as taking place much later: “If you deduct 1656 from Archbishop Usher’s date for creation, 4004 BC, the date
for Noah’s Flood would be around 2348 BC. It’s not possible to narrow down the date further.”37 If this is the case,
then the Lord’s return is well over 500 years away! This would also conflict with the 6k-1k model. Granted, if the
genealogies have gaps within them, as some creationists allow, with grandfather being listed as father, then the
genealogical record could allow an extra 500 years or so perhaps. As to the 6k-7k model, the 6k may only be an
approximation. On the other hand, computations based on what is actually recorded in the biblical text do lead to a
rather exact computation. Therefore, the 6k might be seen from two vantage points: actual years vs recorded years.
We may have biblical precedence for this type of proposal in Melchizedek. If Shem was Melchizedek, for example,
then we have a record of his genealogy. But the writer of Hebrews says that we do not have a record of
Melchizedek’s genealogy. How do we reconcile the two possibilities? One popular proposal is to suggest that the
writer of Hebrews is using typology in the absence of explicit genealogical records for Melchizedek and the absence
of any explicit connection of Melchizedek with his human counterpart, possibly Shem. The 6k model could be
understood from two different vantage points: First, using exact computation based on recorded genealogies (which
purposefully have been truncated by the divine author) would allow this computation to yield certain results
(produced by those like Krieger) versus a second exact computation based on actual years not recorded by the
biblical data to allow another set of computations (produced by Enoch and Horn). These models would only
converge on the same date, like the crosshairs of the sights of a gun, when seen properly from the two different
vantage points, on the general time frame anticipated by Fortson.

Excursus Regarding Flesh and Blood                                                                             Page 113
       Yet another problem remains with the return-of-the-Nephilim projection. There is another competing way to
interpret the 70 generations predicted by Enoch. Instead of being 70 generations until the second coming of the
Messiah, they could refer to the timing of His first coming. Johnson takes this popular option in his commentary on
Enoch:

            According to Luke 3:23-38, there were seventy generations from Enoch to Jesus Christ. The
      miracles associated with the Azazel ritual performed on Yon Kippur each year stopped when the
      Messiah died on the cross....Jesus made atonement and ascended to heaven. The fallen angels remained
      bound until the seventy generations passed and Christ completed His work. Now they await their last
      judgment, to be cast into the lake of fire.38

As to this miracle, Johnson explains:

              Leviticus describes the Azazel goat being sent into the “wilderness.” But the Mishnah gives
      greater detail about that part of the ritual in Yoma 6. The two goats must be alike in appearance, size,
      and weight. The “wilderness” that the Azazel goat was taken to was actually a ravine twelve miles east
      of Jerusalem. Between Jerusalem and this ravine were ten stations or booths. Since it was a High Holy
      Day, one could not travel very far. One priest took the Azazel goat from Jerusalem to the first booth.
      Then another priest took it from the second to the third booth. This continued until a priest took it from
      the tenth booth to the ravine. Anciently this ravine was called Beit HaDudo. It still exists in the Judean
      desert and is presently called Jabel Muntar. The Mishnah then says the priest took the crimson cord
      off of the goat and tied one piece to the large rock on the cliff of the ravine, and he tied the other piece
      back on to the horns of the goat. He then pushed the goat off the cliff. Before it would be halfway
      down the cliff, it was already torn into pieces.
              If the ritual was properly done, the crimson cord would turn snow white. At that point the priest
      would signal the tenth booth, which would in turn signal the ninth, all the way back to the first booth,
      which would signal the high priest standing at the door of the sanctuary. When the high priest learned
      the crimson thread had turned white, he finished the ritual by quoting the prophet Isaiah.39

       Once again, because of the attractiveness of this interpretation one could dismiss the eschatological
interpretation of the Enochian generations. Or one could argue that both interpretations are correct. In acquiescence
to the principle of duality which is seen so often in prophecy, I am willing to allow the possibility of a dual
applicability. Indeed, trying to limit oneself to one frame of reference seems particularly ill-advised in making these
mathematical projections. For example, one glaring weakness with some of the above computations is that they
presume that a generation is 70-80 years, which is not always the case. Depending upon the context, a generation
might be computed to be 120 years (Gen 6:3), 100 years (Gen 15:13), 70-80 years (Ps 95:10), or 40 years
(Num 32:13). Interestingly, though, Peck shows that all these computations for various generational lengths and the
50-year cycle for the Jubilee year have a point of convergence in 2017-2018. “All these things and more seem to
be pointing to the years 2017-2018 as a significant time in the near future. It would seem, if history repeats itself,
we might see a major event in Israel.”40 Hopefully, we only have another year or two before we will have
experiential confirmation as to which model is correct, both prophetically and misthologically.
